< text>
I completed my doctorate at GGU and it was an incredibly rewarding experience.  I was first drawn to the program because it was the only fully-accredited doctorate in finance in the Bay Area that could be pursued part-time by someone who also had a career. The experience proved to be so much more than that, however..  The full-time faculty who run the program are passionate about what they do, offering students the opportunity to engage in significant personal growth and deep learning. The faculty are also well suited to GGU's mission, combining, as they do, first class academic credentials with significant leadership experience in the "real world."

There are two distinct phases to doctoral study and GGU's program delivers the best of both.  The first phase is focused on core doctoral seminars that provide the tools and conceptual framework for understanding and conducting formal research. It was here that I came to fully appreciate the nature of the academic enterprise and begin to master the tools and techniques for its pursuit.

The second phase involves the development of a research question that will result (if you're sufficiently diligent) in the production of a formal dissertation.  This is the apprenticeship phase, where you work closely with your dissertation committee and, most especially, your chair.  My own committee chair, Paul Fouts, was at once both guide and mentor, sending me back again-and-again to reexamine my sources, rewrite my proposals, and revisit the evidence. Each time, my dissertation got better.  In the end, I was able to produce work that I believe will have a real impact on my profession.

The doctoral program is probably the smallest part of what GGU does, but it represents the best of the University's mission and values. Beyond that,  I can heartily recommend GGU to anyone who seeks to improve their skills and advance their career through any any of the University's many degree and certificate programs.< /text>

<Text>My time here was slightly disappointed.

First, the school's credentials aren't as well recognized compared to the other schools in the area, so many students have a hard time getting a job compared to students from other schools.

Second, the school says they offer help to get students job, but all they do is review your resume and have you go out and find your own opportunities.
Third, the counselors I had for business, kept mixing me up with other students and when it came time to discuss a problem, she'd forget the issue. She also told me I didn't need a class and then said I did. After taking the class, I found out I really didn't have to and wasted an entire semester with this school.
Fourth, the resources may seem like alot at first, but the truth is, what really matters are resources for certifications. They don't have many resources that'll help and do not offer certifications for most programs.
Fifth,  the teachers and systems aren't as reliable. I find that some professors don't like it when you have questions. Some make you go to class to listen to the lecture and then still make you do an entire online course (might as well do online only). Some have a power trip and would make excuses for being late on grading or make "adjustments" to their grading on the syllabus after class is finished, messing up your entire semester. Most teachers are never up to date on their online courses. They either don't fix the dates for due dates or they don't open the assignments or just not clear on their direction.

Sixth, there are a lot of students that are international here that get discriminated against. It's very disheartening when they have to report that their teachers are saying rude remarks or making jokes about anyone of color.

Bottom line is, I regret coming here. While there were some great teachers, there weren't enough to count past one hand. Don't make the same mistake as I did. Get your money's worth elsewhere.</Text>< time>

I had the most traumatic experience at Paul Revere and so did my best friends. I held my tongue as a child because I didn't know any better. Now as an adult I would like to write to review on behalf of all voiceless children. I graduated in 2004.This school was beyond corrupt. I will write on some of my own personal experiences. For one, the staff did not care about students being bullied. I was psychically attached by over 20 other children. I suffer from sever neck problems till this day. Instead of the staff having sympathy for me, they suspended me for pushing them off of me, which they considered hitting back. That is self defense. They also blamed it on me and said that it was because I dress too nice, and those kids were bussed in from less affluent areas. There was a teacher's helper named "Mr. Cool" that never revealed him name. He was a pedophile. I complained with about 5 other females that we were uncomfortable because he would hid on us, try to look down our shirts, and write us love notes. The school counselor told us we did not have proof. When the teacher found out she pulled me aside and yelled at me that I "need to grow up and realize daddy isn't the only man in my life" and that I need to back off because she needs his help in class." I was only 12 years old. There was also a teacher named of Mr. Carnine. He once yelled at me in class off the top of his lungs, in my face that I am a RETARD and never going to go anywhere in life. This was because I had a small learning disorder. Till this day it makes me tear up when I think of it, and I wish that I would have complained. It is one of my biggest regrets till this day. I remember the whole class feeling sorry for me. He also came to a teacher, parent  conference and said that whoever thinks I am getting into college is delusional. If Mr. Carnine is reading this I would like him to know that I graduated college with a 4.0 GPA. Please do not send your kids to this institution. Don't be fooled by the nice neighborhood and such.<//Review>

< Text>
An absolutely lovely locale with seating choices offering you the opportunity to literally put your toes in the sand. Offshore breezes, the smell of the ocean, and people watching galore make this an excellent location! The menu choices are somewhat limited and a little too self consciously healthy for my choice, but the food was delicious and impeccably prepared. Pricing was expensive, but given the locale that's to be expected. Service was somewhat sparse and could charitably be called "relaxed" and "unhurried."</Text>

<review>Looking for a comfy, informal option to get breakfast, lunch or a beverage on the beach? This is the spot. It's away from most of the intense touristy areas closer to the pier, but still within view and easy to get to. The most difficult part is finding a place to park. The parking trick: if there isn't one immediately available, just patiently wait for a few minutes and a space will open up. They have seating on the beach (semi shaded) or inside.  The food is healthy, well sourced/prepared and nicely presented. There's also a great playground next door for the kids to explore.<//review>< pictures>

5< /Rate>
< Text>
When a restaurant is right on the sand, as this one is, it doesn't have to be good.

And this one isn't... just good. It's GREAT!

Went there for brunch with my friend Judi from San Francisco (you know her, right, fun gal). I figured that people from up north would be happy to be on a beach that wasn't like the arctic tundra... and there's easy (if NOT free) parking.

I was right. they loved it. But, what surprised me, was how much I loved it, too!

The waitress was tanned and friendly, the food arrived quickly, and we were all amazed at how good it was. "Amazed" is an overused word, but in this case, we literally were.

I had the brisket hash, which is like corned beef has but with... you got it. Beef brisket, sunny side up eggs, piquillo peppers, caramelized onions, horseradish crema.

The brisket was lean, tender, delicious. The piquillo peppers are flavorful without being spicy (I'm sensitive to heat and this delicious wasn't hot). The eggs were perfectly cooked, and the horseradish crema was a licious addition.

Judi had a Market omelet with butternut squash, caramelized onion and she raved about it. Her husband had the Nutella french toast and it was gone before I could taste it!

A quintessentially LA experience - highly recommended!</Text>
